The definition of the word "yachted" is to travel on a yacht or engage in the activity of owning and operating a yacht. The infinitive form of this verb is "to yacht". Here are all the conjugations for this verb:

- I yacht, you yacht, he/she/it yachts (present tense)
- I yachted, you yachted, he/she/it yachted (past tense)
- I have yachted, you have yachted, he/she/it has yachted (present perfect tense)
- I had yachted, you had yachted, he/she/it had yachted (past perfect tense)
- I am yachting, you are yachting, he/she/it is yachting (present continuous tense)

"language_origin": "English",

"topic_area": "Historical, Social"
}

"Yeomanhood" refers to the condition or quality of being a yeoman, which was a social class in medieval England and later in early modern Europe denoting a free farmer possessing a small or moderate-sized landholding. The term came to be used metonymically for the class as a whole.

Singular: yeomanhood
Plural: yeomenhood or yeomanries (historical context) or yeomen (modern usage)

Explanation:
The word "you've" is an auxiliary verb in English language. It is formed by combining the pronoun "you" with the auxiliary verb "have". This form is used to indicate the present perfect tense. Since it is an auxiliary verb, it does not have an infinitive form or any conjugations of its own, but rather functions as a helper for other verbs in a sentence. It is a common word in English language and is used extensively in spoken and written English.
